### III.G. Debt Covenants & Financial Compliance Framework: Operational Restrictions and Default Triggers

American Sustainability Partners' acquisition financing credit agreement (projected execution February 2025) imposes **comprehensive negative covenants** restricting United Environmental Services Corporation's operational flexibility through (1) **financial maintenance covenants** requiring quarterly compliance with maximum leverage ratios (6.0× Total Net Leverage stepping down from Year 1 10.0× and 4.5× Senior Secured Leverage), (2) **incurrence-based restrictions** on debt, liens, investments, and asset sales requiring explicit lender consent or satisfaction of financial condition tests, and (3) **affirmative covenants** mandating periodic financial reporting, insurance maintenance, and compliance certifications,¹⁶²⁸ collectively creating **narrow operating corridor** where covenant breach triggers (a) immediate cross-default across all $3.0 billion debt facilities, (b) automatic termination of $400 million revolving credit commitments eliminating contingent liquidity access, (c) acceleration rights permitting administrative agent to declare entire principal balance immediately due and payable, and (d) enforcement remedies including foreclosure on first lien collateral valued at $1.2 billion liquidation estimate (65% recovery rate on $1.85 billion pledged asset base).¹⁶²⁹ The covenant framework's **stepped compliance requirements** escalate restrictiveness over 5-year term with Year 1-2 permitting elevated leverage and limited operational constraints to accommodate integration period, followed by **progressive tightening** in Years 3-5 mandating deleveraging through EBITDA growth or debt paydown with failure triggering **technical default** even absent payment default, distinguishing technical covenant violation (curable through amendment/waiver process averaging $5-8 million fees plus 75-100 bps interest rate increases) from payment default (immediate acceleration without cure period).¹⁶³⁰ United Environmental Services Corporation's current 2.8× leverage ratio under existing $892 million debt structure provides **comfortable 3.2× cushion** below 6.0× maintenance covenant maximum, but American Sustainability Partners' proposed acquisition financing producing 9.5× pro forma leverage **eliminates covenant cushion entirely**, requiring (1) negotiation of higher Year 1-2 covenant levels (10.0× Year 1 vs. standard 6.0× immediate), (2) maximization of Adjusted EBITDA definitional addbacks (up to $246 million for transaction costs, synergies, non-recurring expenses permitting pro forma 5.3× leverage calculation from 9.5× reported), or (3) immediate operational improvement generating $185 million incremental EBITDA within 12 months to restore covenant compliance margins, creating **HIGH FINANCIAL COMPLIANCE RISK** throughout Year 1-2 integration period when covenant cushions compressed to 10-15% implying **single missed quarterly target triggers breach** without room for normal business volatility.¹⁶³¹

#### III.G.1. Financial Maintenance Covenants: Leverage Ratios and Calculation Mechanics

The credit agreement's financial maintenance covenants impose two quarterly-tested leverage restrictions defining maximum permitted debt levels relative to EBITDA generation, calculated using **Adjusted EBITDA** definition permitting specified addbacks and **Total Debt** and **Senior Secured Debt** definitions excluding certain obligations:

**Maximum Total Net Leverage Ratio Covenant**

| Covenant Component | Definition | Application to Pro Forma Capital Structure |
|--------------------|------------|-------------------------------------------|
| **Total Debt** | All borrowed money obligations including Term Loan B, Revolver drawn amounts, equipment financing, capital leases, and guarantee obligations | $3,000M ($1,700M Term Loan + $400M Revolver commitment of which $0 initially drawn + $900M equipment financing assumed without payoff) |
| **Less: Cash** | Unrestricted cash and cash equivalents, capped at lesser of (a) $50M or (b) 5% of Total Debt | $(50M) maximum credit (actual $100M balance sheet cash but covenant caps benefit at $50M) |
| **Net Debt** | Total Debt minus capped Cash | $2,950M ($3,000M - $50M cap) |
| **Adjusted EBITDA** | Trailing twelve-month EBITDA with permitted addbacks (see Adjusted EBITDA definition below) | $315M reported + up to $246M addbacks = $561M maximum covenant EBITDA |
| **Total Net Leverage Ratio** | Net Debt ÷ Adjusted EBITDA | **9.4× reported basis** ($2,950M ÷ $315M) or **5.3× adjusted basis** ($2,950M ÷ $561M maximum EBITDA) |
| **Maximum Covenant Level** | Stepped schedule over 5-year term | Year 1: 10.0×, Year 2: 8.5×, Year 3: 7.0×, Year 4-5: 6.0× |
| **Compliance Test** | Calculated quarterly as of last day of fiscal quarter | Tested Q2 2025, Q3 2025, Q4 2025, etc. (one quarter after closing in Q1 2025) |
| **Cure Rights** | Equity contribution permitted to reduce leverage ratio | ASP may contribute equity counted as EBITDA for covenant purposes (see §III.G.4) |

The Total Net Leverage covenant's **$50 million cash cap** prevents borrowers from artificially improving leverage ratios through accumulating balance sheet cash without debt paydown, ensuring **meaningful deleveraging** requires either EBITDA growth or principal reduction.¹⁶³² The cap's practical impact: UESC's pro forma $100 million closing cash receives only $50 million covenant credit, worsening reported leverage from 9.3× (with full cash offset) to 9.4× (with capped offset), though difference is immaterial relative to 10.0× Year 1 maximum.¹⁶³³ The cash cap also **incentivizes debt paydown over cash accumulation** as every dollar of debt reduction improves leverage ratio by $1 numerator decrease while cash accumulation beyond $50 million provides no covenant benefit, steering management toward aggressive deleveraging strategies rather than liquidity hoarding.¹⁶³⁴

The covenant's **stepped maximum levels** reflecting integration period accommodation through Year 1-2 elevated tolerance (10.0× and 8.5×) followed by mandatory deleveraging in Years 3-5 (7.0× and 6.0×) establish **contractual deleveraging pathway** requiring minimum debt reduction or EBITDA growth to maintain compliance:

| Compliance Period | Maximum Total Net Leverage | Implied Minimum EBITDA at $2,950M Net Debt | Required EBITDA Growth from $315M Baseline | Implied Debt Paydown Alternative (at $315M EBITDA) |
|-------------------|---------------------------|-------------------------------------------|-------------------------------------------|---------------------------------------------------|
| **Year 1 (Q1-Q4 2025)** | 10.0× | $295M | None (6% below current) | $0 (current leverage 9.4×) |
| **Year 2 (2026)** | 8.5× | $347M | $32M (10% growth) | $270M paydown to $2,680M |
| **Year 3 (2027)** | 7.0× | $421M | $106M (34% growth) | $852M paydown to $2,098M |
| **Year 4 (2028)** | 6.0× | $492M | $177M (56% growth) | $1,060M paydown to $1,890M |
| **Year 5+ (2029+)** | 6.0× | $492M | $177M (maintained) | $1,060M (maintained) |

The deleveraging requirements' **magnitude** (requiring $177M EBITDA growth representing 56% improvement over 4 years or $1.06B debt paydown representing 36% principal reduction) substantially exceed UESC's historical performance (6.1% EBITDA CAGR 2019-2024) and typical free cash flow generation ($172M annually insufficient for $265M average annual debt paydown required), indicating covenant compliance pathway depends **critically on operational improvement plan execution** delivering $154M EBITDA expansion as detailed in §III.F.5 or **strategic alternative** such as asset sales generating $450-520M proceeds applied to debt paydown.¹⁶³⁵

**Maximum Senior Secured Leverage Ratio Covenant**

| Covenant Component | Definition | Pro Forma Calculation |
|--------------------|------------|----------------------|
| **Senior Secured Debt** | All secured obligations including Term Loan B, Revolver, equipment financing (but excluding unsecured debt, subordinated obligations) | $3,000M (100% of debt is senior secured; no unsecured layer in capital structure) |
| **Adjusted EBITDA** | Identical to Total Net Leverage calculation | $315M reported + up to $246M addbacks = $561M maximum |
| **Senior Secured Leverage Ratio** | Senior Secured Debt ÷ Adjusted EBITDA | **9.5× reported** ($3,000M ÷ $315M) or **5.3× adjusted** ($3,000M ÷ $561M) |
| **Maximum Covenant Level** | Stepped schedule | Year 1: 6.5×, Year 2: 5.5×, Year 3: 4.75×, Year 4-5: 4.5× |
| **Practical Impact** | More restrictive than Total Net Leverage due to lower maximum ratios | **Binding covenant** in Years 1-3 (Senior Secured more restrictive than Total Net) |
| **Revolver Access Control** | Breach suspends revolver availability even if commitments outstanding | Creates liquidity crisis risk if covenant violated |

The Senior Secured Leverage covenant serves as **revolver availability gatekeeper** with breach automatically suspending borrowing availability under $400 million commitment even if facility otherwise undrawn, creating **liquidity crisis risk** where covenant breach coincides with operational cash needs forcing working capital constraints.¹⁶³⁶ The covenant's **more restrictive maximum levels** compared to Total Net Leverage (4.5× vs. 6.0× long-term) reflects lenders' **priority concern** about senior secured debt burden since senior secured obligations rank ahead of unsecured claims in bankruptcy distribution, with lower maximum ensuring adequate asset coverage (implied 4.5× Senior Secured Leverage produces $4.50 debt per $1.00 EBITDA, or approximately 2.2× debt-to-asset ratio assuming 2.0× EBITDA-to-asset valuation multiple, providing 45% loan-to-value coverage).¹⁶³⁷

**Adjusted EBITDA Definition: Permitted Addbacks and Calculation Examples**

The leverage covenant calculations permit **Adjusted EBITDA** exceeding reported EBITDA through five categories of addbacks, subject to aggregate cap of **25% of Pro Forma EBITDA** for forward-looking adjustments (synergies, cost savings) and unlimited addbacks for historical non-recurring expenses and transaction costs:

**Category 1: Transaction Costs and Expenses**
- *Permitted:* All fees, costs, and expenses incurred in connection with acquisition, financing, and related transactions including investment banking fees ($54M), legal/advisory fees ($38M), financing fees/OID ($24M), change-of-control penalties ($4M)
- *Limitation:* One-time addback in quarter incurred (Q1 2025 for ASP acquisition)
- *Pro Forma Impact:* **+$120M EBITDA addback** for Q1 2025, declining to $0 in Q2 2025 and thereafter as TTM calculation rolls forward
- *Compliance Benefit:* Reduces Q1 2025 pro forma leverage from 9.4× to 7.7× ($2,950M ÷ $385M), providing 2.3× cushion below 10.0× Year 1 maximum

**Category 2: Cost Savings, Operating Expense Reductions, and Synergies**
- *Permitted:* Run-rate cost savings and synergies projected to be realized within 18 months of measurement date, calculated on pro forma basis as if realized at measurement date
- *Limitation:* Aggregate amount not to exceed 25% of Pro Forma EBITDA ($315M × 25% = $79M maximum)
- *Documentation Requirements:* Factual basis for projected savings, reasonable detail supporting calculations, officer's certificate certifying amounts
- *Pro Forma Impact:* **+$79M EBITDA addback** maximum for operational improvement initiatives detailed in §III.F.5 (route optimization $38M, labor management $29M, MRF optimization $10M, pricing discipline $23M less $21M allocated to other categories = $79M)
- *Compliance Benefit:* Further reduces pro forma leverage from 7.7× to 6.5× ($2,950M ÷ $454M), providing 3.5× cushion below 10.0× Year 1 maximum
- *Controversy Risk:* MEDIUM - lenders frequently challenge synergy addbacks as speculative, requiring robust documentation and may result in negotiated haircut to 60-75% of projected amounts in amendment scenarios

**Category 3: Non-Recurring Expenses**
- *Permitted:* Unusual, non-recurring, or extraordinary expenses including restructuring charges, integration costs, severance payments, facility closure costs, asset impairments (all with reasonable detail)
- *Limitation:* Aggregate amount not to exceed 15% of Pro Forma EBITDA ($315M × 15% = $47M maximum)
- *Pro Forma Impact:* **+$47M EBITDA addback** for anticipated integration costs (IT system integration $18M, facility rationalization $12M, rebranding $7M, redundant personnel severance $10M)
- *Compliance Benefit:* Reduces pro forma leverage from 6.5× to 5.9× ($2,950M ÷ $501M), providing 4.1× cushion below 10.0× Year 1 maximum
- *Audit Risk:* LOW - historical expenses are verifiable and documented, reducing lender challenge risk

**Category 4: Equity-Based Compensation**
- *Permitted:* Stock option expense, restricted stock amortization, and other non-cash equity compensation
- *Limitation:* Actual amounts incurred (no cap)
- *Pro Forma Impact:* **+$8M EBITDA addback** for ASP management equity incentive program ($5.2M annual grant date fair value amortization + $2.8M rollover UESC management equity)
- *Accounting Treatment:* ASC 718 requires expense recognition for equity compensation but covenant addback eliminates impact on financial covenant calculations

**Category 5: Purchase Accounting Adjustments**
- *Permitted:* Adjustments related to purchase accounting including inventory step-up amortization, backlog amortization, customer relationship amortization
- *Limitation:* Actual amounts for 12 months post-acquisition
- *Pro Forma Impact:* **$0 in stock purchase** (ASP acquiring UESC stock without asset step-up, eliminating purchase accounting impacts that would arise in asset purchase; this represents $35-50M lost addback opportunity versus asset structure)
- *Strategic Consideration:* Stock purchase elected for tax reasons (avoiding corporate-level gain recognition) but sacrifices covenant flexibility that asset purchase would provide through step-up amortization addbacks

**Aggregate Adjusted EBITDA Calculation (Q1 2025 Pro Forma Example)**

| EBITDA Component | Amount ($ millions) | Explanation |
|------------------|---------------------|-------------|
| **Reported EBITDA (TTM Q1 2025)** | $315 | UESC standalone trailing twelve-month EBITDA |
| **+Transaction Costs** | $120 | One-time closing costs (Q1 2025 only) |
| **+Cost Savings/Synergies** | $79 | Run-rate operational improvements (capped at 25%) |
| **+Non-Recurring Expenses** | $47 | Integration costs (capped at 15%) |
| **+Equity Compensation** | $8 | Non-cash management incentives |
| **+Purchase Accounting** | $0 | Not applicable (stock purchase) |
| **=Adjusted EBITDA (Maximum)** | **$569** | Maximum covenant EBITDA with all addbacks |
| **Pro Forma Leverage Ratio** | **5.2×** | $2,950M Net Debt ÷ $569M Adjusted EBITDA |
| **Year 1 Covenant Maximum** | **10.0×** | Compliance cushion: **4.8 turns** (92% margin) |

The maximum Adjusted EBITDA calculation producing **$569 million covenant EBITDA** (81% above $315M reported EBITDA) provides **substantial covenant relief** in Year 1, reducing pro forma leverage from 9.4× reported to 5.2× adjusted and creating 4.8× compliance cushion below 10.0× maximum.¹⁶³⁸ However, the addbacks' **declining benefit over time** as transaction costs roll out of TTM calculation (Q2 2025) and synergies transition from projected to actual (requiring realization to maintain addback) reduces covenant EBITDA toward reported levels, compressing cushion and increasing breach risk:

| Measurement Date | Transaction Costs in TTM | Synergies (Projected) | Synergies (Realized) | Adjusted EBITDA | Pro Forma Leverage | Covenant Maximum | Cushion |
|------------------|-------------------------|----------------------|---------------------|-----------------|-------------------|------------------|---------|
| **Q1 2025** | $120M (full) | $79M | $0 | $569M | 5.2× | 10.0× | 4.8× |
| **Q2 2025** | $120M | $79M | $18M | $569M | 5.2× | 10.0× | 4.8× |
| **Q3 2025** | $120M | $79M | $42M | $569M | 5.2× | 10.0× | 4.8× |
| **Q4 2025** | $120M | $79M | $68M | $569M | 5.2× | 10.0× | 4.8× |
| **Q1 2026** | $0 (rolled out) | $79M | $87M | $528M | 5.6× | 10.0× | 4.4× |
| **Q2 2026** | $0 | $79M | $108M | $508M | 5.8× | 8.5× | 2.7× |

The Q2 2026 covenant step-down to 8.5× maximum **coincides with transaction cost rollout** reducing Adjusted EBITDA by $120M from $528M (Q1 2026) to $408M (Q2 2026 if no synergies realized), producing **7.2× pro forma leverage** approaching 8.5× maximum and compressing cushion from 4.4× (52% margin) to 1.3× (18% margin), creating **heightened breach risk** if operational improvements underperform even modestly (10% shortfall in synergy realization producing 8.7× leverage exceeding 8.5× maximum by 0.2 turns).¹⁶³⁹

**SECTION III.G.1 STATUS:** Subsection complete. Footnotes: 1628-1639 (12 footnotes). Coverage: Financial maintenance covenants (Total Net Leverage, Senior Secured Leverage), Adjusted EBITDA definition with five addback categories, stepped covenant schedule analysis, covenant cushion trajectory. Remaining III.G subsections: III.G.2 (Incurrence-Based Covenants), III.G.3 (Affirmative Covenants), III.G.4 (Default Events and Cure Mechanisms), III.G.5 (Priority Finding Summary). #### III.G.2. Incurrence-Based Covenants: Operational Restrictions and Strategic Flexibility Constraints

The credit agreement imposes **comprehensive incurrence-based negative covenants** restricting United Environmental Services Corporation's ability to undertake specified actions without (1) prior written consent from Required Lenders (lenders holding more than 50% of outstanding commitments and loans under the facilities), or (2) satisfaction of **financial condition tests** permitting specified "baskets" of otherwise-prohibited activities, creating **material constraints on American Sustainability Partners' post-acquisition strategic flexibility** including limitations on bolt-on acquisitions, dividend distributions to ASP equity holders, asset monetization, and incremental debt financing.¹⁶⁴⁰

**Debt Incurrence Restrictions**

The credit agreement prohibits UESC and its subsidiaries from incurring, creating, assuming, or guaranteeing any additional indebtedness beyond amounts outstanding on the closing date, subject to the following permitted indebtedness baskets allowing limited incremental borrowing without lender consent:¹⁶⁴¹

| Basket Type | Permitted Amount/Test | Application to Pro Forma Structure | Strategic Impact |
|-------------|----------------------|-------------------------------------|------------------|
| **Revolving Credit Facility** | Up to commitment amount ($400M) | $0 drawn at closing; full availability for working capital and letters of credit | Preserves liquidity for operational needs but does not permit incremental term debt |
| **Ratio Debt Basket** | Unlimited if Pro Forma Total Net Leverage ≤6.0× after giving effect to incurrence | **Unavailable until Year 4** (pro forma 9.2× actual leverage in Year 1 declining to 6.0× by Q4 2028 per covenant schedule) | Blocks incremental financing during 36-month integration window when operational improvements are most capital-intensive |
| **General Basket** | Greater of (a) $50M or (b) 7.5% of Consolidated Total Assets (~$240M based on $3.2B asset base) | $240M incremental debt capacity without financial test | Provides limited flexibility for equipment financing or small refinancings but insufficient for material acquisitions |
| **Purchase Money Debt** | Up to $75M outstanding at any time for equipment, vehicles, or real property acquisitions | Secured only by purchased assets, no cross-collateralization | Supports fleet replacement but requires asset-specific lender approval and appraisals |
| **Intercompany Debt** | Unlimited between UESC and wholly-owned subsidiaries | Subject to subordination requirements if borrower is non-guarantor subsidiary | Enables internal cash management but does not provide external financing capacity |
| **Permitted Refinancing Debt** | Refinancing of existing Term Loan B or Revolver on equivalent or more favorable terms | Requires no increase in principal, no shortened maturity, no additional collateral | Allows opportunistic refinancing if credit markets improve but does not permit balance sheet expansion |

The **Ratio Debt Basket** represents the primary incremental financing capacity under the credit agreement, permitting unlimited additional indebtedness if UESC can demonstrate Pro Forma Total Net Leverage of 6.0× or less after giving effect to the new borrowing and application of proceeds.¹⁶⁴² However, this basket is **functionally unavailable during the critical 36-month post-acquisition integration period** due to the company's 9.2× actual pro forma leverage at closing (before Adjusted EBITDA addbacks) declining to 8.1× in Year 2 and 7.2× in Year 3, reaching the 6.0× threshold only in Q4 2028 assuming (1) full achievement of $154M in risk-adjusted operational improvements, (2) application of 100% of excess cash flow to mandatory prepayments, and (3) no material adverse developments in municipal solid waste volumes or commodity pricing.¹⁶⁴³ This **36-month financing blackout period** coincides precisely with the window during which American Sustainability Partners is most likely to pursue bolt-on acquisitions to achieve revenue synergies, capture additional market share in fragmented regional markets, and realize operational efficiencies through route density optimization and shared services consolidation.¹⁶⁴⁴

**Lien Restrictions**

The credit agreement prohibits UESC and its subsidiaries from creating, incurring, or permitting any lien, security interest, or encumbrance on any asset, subject to the following permitted lien categories:¹⁶⁴⁵

| Lien Category | Scope | Application to Pro Forma Structure | Remaining Capacity |
|---------------|-------|-------------------------------------|-------------------|
| **Credit Agreement Liens** | First-priority perfected liens on substantially all assets securing Term Loan B and Revolver | Blanket lien on (1) all accounts receivable, inventory, equipment, vehicles, real property, IP, and general intangibles, (2) 100% equity interests in all subsidiaries | **Zero unencumbered assets** available as collateral for incremental financing or DIP financing in distress scenarios |
| **Purchase Money Liens** | Liens securing Purchase Money Debt on acquired equipment/vehicles only | Limited to financed asset with loan-to-value not exceeding 100% of cost | Subordinated to Credit Agreement Liens; requires intercreditor agreement approval from administrative agent |
| **Permitted Encumbrances** | Statutory liens (taxes, mechanics liens), easements, rights-of-way, zoning restrictions | Ordinary course items not materially impairing asset value or business operations | Non-discretionary; arise by operation of law |
| **Ratio Lien Basket** | Liens securing Ratio Debt Basket borrowings if Pro Forma Total Net Leverage ≤6.0× | Pari passu with Credit Agreement Liens subject to intercreditor agreement | Unavailable until Year 4 due to leverage levels (same constraint as Ratio Debt Basket) |
| **Liens on Non-Guarantor Subsidiaries** | Liens on assets of non-guarantor subsidiaries (primarily international operations and certain special-purpose entities) | Limited to ~$180M of assets at non-guarantor subs representing 5.6% of consolidated asset base | Provides minimal strategic flexibility given immateriality of non-guarantor operations |

The **comprehensive first-priority lien** granted to Term Loan B and Revolver lenders on substantially all UESC assets eliminates the availability of **unencumbered assets for debtor-in-possession (DIP) financing** in the event of financial distress requiring Chapter 11 bankruptcy protection.¹⁶⁴⁶ Under 11 U.S.C. § 364(c) and (d), a debtor may obtain DIP financing with priority over existing secured creditors only if (1) existing secured creditors consent, (2) existing secured creditors are adequately protected, or (3) the debtor demonstrates that credit is unavailable on any other terms and existing creditors' interests are not materially prejudiced.¹⁶⁴⁷ In practice, **blanket first-priority liens severely limit DIP financing availability** because (1) prospective DIP lenders are unwilling to accept junior lien positions given high loss severity rates on second-lien debt in bankruptcy (50-70% recovery vs. 80-90% for first-lien), (2) existing first-lien lenders typically refuse to consent to priming liens absent substantial adequacy protection payments, and (3) bankruptcy courts are reluctant to approve priming liens without secured creditor consent except in cases of imminent liquidation risk.¹⁶⁴⁸ UESC's **comprehensive asset encumbrance** therefore **reduces strategic flexibility in distress scenarios**, potentially forcing the company to accept less favorable terms in out-of-court restructurings or limiting its ability to fund operations during a bankruptcy proceeding.¹⁶⁴⁹

**Investment and Acquisition Restrictions**

The credit agreement prohibits UESC and its subsidiaries from making any investment in, or acquiring any equity interest in, any other person or entity, subject to the following permitted investment baskets:¹⁶⁵⁰

| Investment Basket | Permitted Amount/Test | Application to Bolt-On Acquisition Strategy | Availability Timeline |
|-------------------|----------------------|---------------------------------------------|----------------------|
| **General Investment Basket** | Greater of (a) $75M or (b) 7.5% of Consolidated Total Assets (~$240M) | Sufficient for small tuck-in acquisitions (<$250M enterprise value) but inadequate for material bolt-ons | Available immediately at closing |
| **Ratio Investment Basket** | Unlimited if Pro Forma Total Net Leverage ≤6.0× after giving effect to investment | **Unavailable until Year 4** due to 9.2× actual pro forma leverage declining to 6.0× only by Q4 2028 | Q4 2028 earliest (36-month blackout) |
| **Permitted Acquisitions** | Acquisitions of businesses in same/related line of business if (1) target is solvent, (2) no default exists, (3) acquired entity becomes guarantor | Must use General Investment Basket or Ratio Investment Basket capacity; no separate acquisition carve-out | Subject to basket availability constraints |

American Sustainability Partners' investment thesis contemplates **$800M to $1.2B in bolt-on acquisitions** over a 5-7 year hold period to achieve revenue scale necessary for strategic exit ($5.5B-$6.0B pro forma revenue target vs. $3.7B current), focusing on (1) **regional solid waste collection platforms** in underpenetrated markets where UESC lacks density, (2) **materials recovery facilities and recycling assets** to capture commodity upside and diversify revenue streams, and (3) **C&D processing facilities** to enter the commercial construction waste segment representing 35-40% of total waste generation but only 18% of UESC's current revenue mix.¹⁶⁵¹ However, the credit agreement's investment restrictions impose **severe constraints on acquisition timing and sizing**:

**Case Study: Hypothetical Regional Acquisition**

Consider a **$240M acquisition** of a regional solid waste collection platform in the Pacific Northwest market (Portland/Seattle MSAs) with $180M revenue, $54M EBITDA (30% margin reflecting lower route density and higher labor costs than UESC's 16.8% baseline margin), and strategic fit due to (1) minimal geographic overlap with UESC's existing footprint (only 8% customer overlap), (2) complementary service mix (65% residential collection vs. UESC's 45% residential, 42% commercial), and (3) operational improvement potential through route optimization, back-office consolidation, and fleet standardization projected to generate $12M annual run-rate synergies (22% of target EBITDA) within 24 months:¹⁶⁵²

| Acquisition Metric | Amount | Financing Approach Under Credit Agreement | Constraint Impact |
|-------------------|--------|-------------------------------------------|------------------|
| **Purchase Price** | $240M (4.4× target EBITDA) | Must use General Investment Basket ($240M available) | Consumes 100% of basket capacity for single transaction |
| **Transaction Costs** | $12M (5% of EV for advisory, legal, diligence, integration planning) | Not counted in Investment Basket but increases total cash outlay | Requires use of Revolver or operating cash |
| **Working Capital Adjustment** | $8M (estimated for AR/AP settlement) | Additional cash required at closing | Further draws on Revolver availability |
| **Total Cash Required** | $260M | **Exceeds General Investment Basket** by $20M | Cannot complete transaction without Ratio Investment Basket access (unavailable until Year 4) or lender amendment consent |
| **Financing Sources** | (1) $240M General Investment Basket, (2) $20M Revolver draw | Revolver has $400M availability but $20M draw reduces liquidity cushion | Transaction is **technically permissible** but requires use of working capital facility for strategic acquisition |
| **Impact on Covenant Compliance** | Pro forma EBITDA increases by $54M (target) + $12M (synergies) = $66M; leverage decreases from 9.2× to 8.7× (modest improvement) | Improves financial covenant compliance trajectory | Acquisition is **covenant-enhancing** but basket constraints prevent execution of similar follow-on transactions |

This example demonstrates that even **covenant-enhancing bolt-on acquisitions** improving UESC's leverage profile and business diversification are **severely constrained by investment basket limitations** during the 36-month integration window when ASP is most likely to pursue organic and inorganic growth initiatives.¹⁶⁵³ The **inability to access Ratio Investment Basket capacity** until Year 4 effectively **forces American Sustainability Partners into a purely organic growth strategy** during Years 1-3, limiting revenue CAGR to 3-5% (market growth plus modest pricing) vs. the 8-12% target return profile underwriting that assumes $800M+ in acquisitions contributing 300-500 bps of annual growth.¹⁶⁵⁴

**Asset Sale and Disposition Restrictions**

The credit agreement prohibits UESC and its subsidiaries from selling, transferring, or disposing of any asset or property outside the ordinary course of business (defined as sales of obsolete equipment, worn-out vehicles, or inventory in the normal course not exceeding $25M annually in aggregate), subject to **mandatory prepayment requirements** for any material asset sales:¹⁶⁵⁵

| Asset Disposition Type | Permitted Without Consent | Mandatory Prepayment Requirement | Application to ASP Divestiture Strategy |
|------------------------|---------------------------|----------------------------------|----------------------------------------|
| **Non-Strategic Asset Sales** | Sales generating up to $50M gross proceeds in any fiscal year | 100% of net proceeds (after taxes, costs, reinvestment in business within 365 days) applied to Term Loan B prepayment | Eliminates ability to use divestiture proceeds for debt repayment flexibility or return of capital to sponsors |
| **Strategic Business Divestitures** | Requires Required Lenders consent (>50% approval) | 100% of net proceeds applied to Term Loan B prepayment unless reinvested in permitted acquisitions/capex within 365 days | Blocks ASP's contemplated **$450M transfer station divestiture** unless (1) lenders consent, (2) proceeds used for debt paydown, or (3) proceeds reinvested in qualifying uses |
| **Sale-Leaseback Transactions** | Permitted for real property up to $100M in aggregate if (1) fair market value lease terms, (2) 15-year maximum lease term, (3) leaseback classified as operating lease under GAAP | Deemed asset sale; net proceeds subject to mandatory prepayment | Provides limited liquidity option but insufficient for material financing needs |
| **Involuntary Dispositions** | Casualty events, condemnation, eminent domain not subject to consent requirements | Insurance/condemnation proceeds exceeding $25M applied to Term Loan B unless reinvested in repair/replacement within 365 days | Lenders control casualty proceeds; restricts business continuity financing flexibility |

American Sustainability Partners' base-case business plan contemplates **divesting $450M of non-core transfer station assets** in Years 2-3 to (1) reduce leverage by 1.4× from 9.2× to 7.8× through debt prepayment, (2) simplify operational complexity by exiting 15 underperforming transfer stations with sub-10% ROIC, and (3) focus management attention on higher-return collection and processing operations.¹⁶⁵⁶ However, the credit agreement's **100% mandatory prepayment requirement** means that **all $450M in net divestiture proceeds** (after taxes and transaction costs) must be applied to Term Loan B principal reduction, with **zero ability to redeploy capital** into higher-return bolt-on acquisitions, capex investments in MRF automation, or distributions to ASP equity holders.¹⁶⁵⁷ This **mandatory application requirement eliminates strategic flexibility** to optimize capital allocation, effectively converting the divestiture program into a **lender-directed deleveraging mechanism** rather than a sponsor-controlled asset rotation strategy.¹⁶⁵⁸

The **365-day reinvestment window** provides theoretical flexibility to avoid prepayment by reinvesting proceeds in permitted acquisitions or capital expenditures, but this option is **practically unavailable** during Years 1-3 due to (1) Ratio Investment Basket unavailability blocking material acquisitions (as analyzed above), and (2) maintenance capex requirements (~$140M annually) already funded from operating cash flow without need for divestiture proceeds, leaving **no qualifying reinvestment uses** for the $450M of asset sale proceeds.¹⁶⁵⁹

**Restricted Payments and Dividend Limitations**

The credit agreement prohibits UESC from making any restricted payment, defined as (1) cash dividends or distributions on equity interests, (2) redemptions or repurchases of equity interests, (3) payments on subordinated debt, or (4) investments in unrestricted subsidiaries, subject to the following permitted payment baskets:¹⁶⁶⁰

| Restricted Payment Type | Permitted Amount/Test | Application to ASP Return of Capital | Annual Capacity | Effective Yield to ASP |
|-------------------------|----------------------|--------------------------------------|----------------|----------------------|
| **Builder Basket** | Greater of (a) $30M or (b) 2% of Consolidated Total Assets (~$64M based on $3.2B asset base), cumulative from closing | $64M immediately available increasing by $64M per year, subject to no default | **$64M Year 1** increasing to $128M cumulative Year 2, $192M cumulative Year 3, etc. | 4.3% annual yield on $1.5B equity ($64M / $1.5B) |
| **50% Excess Cash Flow Sweep** | 50% of Excess Cash Flow (defined as EBITDA minus cash interest, cash taxes, capex, changes in working capital) if leverage >6.0× | **Zero capacity** during Years 1-4 due to negative Excess Cash Flow (cash interest $263M > operating cash flow $230M in Year 1) | $0 | 0% yield |
| **Ratio Basket** | Unlimited if Pro Forma Senior Secured Leverage ≤5.5× after giving effect to payment | **Unavailable until Year 5+** (pro forma 9.8× Senior Secured Leverage at closing declining to 5.5× only by 2030+ per covenant schedule) | Year 5+: Potentially $200M+ annual | 13%+ yield in Year 5+ if leverage targets achieved |
| **Management Fees** | Up to $7.5M annually paid to ASP for management, consulting, monitoring, and advisory services | $7.5M immediately available, annual recurring | **$7.5M per year** | 0.5% annual yield on $1.5B equity |

American Sustainability Partners' return expectations assume **7-10% annual cash yield** on its $1.5B equity investment through a combination of dividends, management fees, and transaction fees, consistent with the firm's target 20-25% gross IRR for middle-market buyout investments (comprising 7-10% yield, 8-12% EBITDA growth, and 3-5% multiple expansion).¹⁶⁶¹ However, the credit agreement's restricted payment provisions **limit ASP to 0.5% annual cash yield** during the 36-month integration period through the $7.5M management fee carve-out, with the **Builder Basket theoretically permitting 4.3% yield** but practically unavailable due to (1) American Sustainability Partners' investment committee policies prohibiting dividend distributions when portfolio companies have leverage exceeding 6.5×, and (2) lender consent requirements for distributions when DSCR falls below 1.1× (actual: 0.88× pro forma).¹⁶⁶²

The effective result is that **American Sustainability Partners receives zero cash return** on its $1.5B equity investment for the first 36-48 months, instead relying entirely on (1) **equity value appreciation** through EBITDA growth and multiple expansion to achieve target returns, and (2) **refinancing or sale proceeds** at exit to realize gains.¹⁶⁶³ This **multi-year cash flow lockup** is **atypical for sponsor-backed LBOs** where dividend recaps, management fee streams, and portfolio company distributions typically provide 3-7% annual cash-on-cash returns to private equity sponsors, and exposes American Sustainability Partners to **heightened exit risk** requiring full recovery of invested capital plus acceptable returns at a single future liquidity event rather than periodic interim cash returns reducing at-risk capital over the hold period.¹⁶⁶⁴

---

**SECTION III.G.2 STATUS:** Subsection complete. Word count: ~2,100 words. Footnotes: 1640-1651 (12 footnotes). Next subsection: III.G.3 (Affirmative Covenants).


#### III.G.3. Affirmative Covenants: Reporting, Insurance, and Compliance Obligations

The credit agreement imposes **comprehensive affirmative covenants** requiring United Environmental Services Corporation to (1) deliver periodic financial statements and compliance certificates demonstrating covenant compliance, (2) maintain specified insurance coverage for property damage, liability exposure, and environmental risks, (3) preserve and perfect lender security interests in collateral through ongoing UCC filings and control agreements, and (4) maintain all material licenses, permits, and regulatory authorizations necessary for business operations, creating **continuous monitoring framework** enabling lenders to detect deteriorating financial condition or regulatory compliance failures triggering acceleration rights.¹⁶⁵²

**Financial Reporting and Compliance Certificate Requirements**

The credit agreement mandates delivery of (1) **quarterly financial statements** within 45 days of quarter-end, consisting of consolidated balance sheet, income statement, cash flow statement, and statement of shareholders' equity, certified by Chief Financial Officer as fairly presenting financial condition in accordance with GAAP (subject to normal year-end adjustments and absence of footnotes), accompanied by **management discussion and analysis** narrative explaining material changes in financial position, (2) **annual audited financial statements** within 90 days of fiscal year-end, audited by independent certified public accountants acceptable to Administrative Agent (currently KPMG LLP), with unqualified audit opinion and complete footnote disclosures required by GAAP, and (3) **compliance certificates** executed by CFO within 5 business days of quarterly and annual statement delivery, demonstrating mathematical compliance with financial covenants through detailed covenant calculation schedules showing Total Net Leverage Ratio, Senior Secured Leverage Ratio, and Adjusted EBITDA reconciliation with line-item detail for all permitted addbacks.¹⁶⁵³ The compliance certificate format requires CFO certification that (a) no Default or Event of Default has occurred or, if occurred, specifying nature and proposed cure action, (b) all representations and warranties in credit agreement remain true and correct in all material respects, and (c) attached covenant calculations are true, correct, and complete, creating **personal certification liability** for CFO under 18 U.S.C. § 1001 (false statements to financial institutions) exposing individual criminal penalties up to $1 million fine and 30 years imprisonment if compliance certificate contains materially false information provided to federally-insured lenders.¹⁶⁵⁴ United Environmental's CFO Richard Morrison faces **heightened certification risk** given (i) aggressive Adjusted EBITDA addback assumptions totaling $254 million requiring subjective judgments on run-rate synergy timing and restructuring charge necessity, (ii) complex covenant calculation mechanics with 47-line EBITDA reconciliation schedule providing multiple opportunities for computational error, and (iii) potential criminal exposure if 2026-2027 financial performance deteriorates below covenant thresholds and ASP management instructs aggressive addback interpretation to avoid technical default, particularly regarding projected synergies not yet realized creating tension between legal compliance and operational reporting.¹⁶⁵⁵

**Insurance Coverage Requirements and Gap Analysis**

The credit agreement requires United Environmental to maintain (1) **property insurance** covering all real and personal property included in borrowing base collateral for full replacement cost value (minimum $2.8 billion aggregate limit based on appraised collateral value), with deductibles not exceeding $5 million per occurrence and naming Administrative Agent as loss payee with lender's loss payable endorsement preventing UESC from collecting proceeds without lender consent, (2) **commercial general liability insurance** with minimum $25 million per-occurrence limit and $50 million annual aggregate, covering bodily injury, property damage, and personal injury claims with pollution liability exclusion requiring separate environmental coverage, (3) **automobile liability insurance** with $10 million combined single limit covering owned, non-owned, and hired vehicles given United Environmental's 847-vehicle collection fleet, (4) **workers' compensation insurance** with statutory limits for all states where UESC maintains employees (42 states currently) plus employer's liability coverage with $5 million limit, (5) **umbrella liability insurance** with $100 million limit providing excess coverage over primary CGL and auto policies, and (6) **environmental impairment liability insurance** with minimum $75 million per-occurrence limit and $150 million annual aggregate, covering sudden and gradual pollution conditions, remediation costs, and third-party bodily injury/property damage claims.¹⁶⁵⁶

United Environmental's current insurance program demonstrates **material coverage gaps** relative to credit agreement requirements and identified environmental liabilities: (1) environmental impairment liability policy provides only $50 million per-occurrence limit (33% shortfall vs. $75 million covenant requirement) with $100 million annual aggregate (also 33% below required $150 million), creating **$25-50 million uninsured exposure** for each major environmental incident, (2) policy contains **Superfund exclusion** eliminating coverage for CERCLA cost recovery actions and contribution claims, directly impairing insurance protection for Michigan Landfill, Ohio River Sediment, and New Jersey Industrial Site matters collectively estimated at $89-267 million, (3) **known loss exclusion** bars coverage for environmental conditions existing prior to policy inception where insured had knowledge of potential claim, potentially excluding all Legacy Site Investigations identified in Section III.D.3 where UESC received EPA information requests or state enforcement notices before current policy period beginning July 1, 2024, (4) property insurance contains **flood exclusion** for facilities located in 100-year floodplain (18 of 127 facilities per FEMA National Flood Insurance Program maps), exposing $347 million in facility replacement cost to uninsured flood damage, and (5) business interruption coverage subject to 72-hour waiting period and 90-day maximum indemnity period, insufficient to cover 6-12 month facility reconstruction timeline for total loss events affecting major processing centers.¹⁶⁵⁷ American Sustainability Partners faces **$156-225 million incremental annual insurance premium cost** to remedy coverage gaps through (i) environmental impairment liability limit increase from $50M to $75M per-occurrence ($8-12 million annual premium increase at 16% rate-on-line), (ii) Superfund coverage buy-back endorsement ($15-25 million annual premium given known CERCLA exposure), (iii) known loss endorsement for Legacy Sites with sublimits and co-insurance ($22-35 million annual premium with 50% co-insurance typical), (iv) flood insurance through NFIP and excess private market ($4-8 million annual), and (v) extended business interruption coverage to 365-day indemnity period ($3-6 million annual premium increase), materially impacting post-acquisition operating margins and potentially triggering covenant compliance issues if insurance expense not contemplated in Adjusted EBITDA addbacks as "non-recurring" cost improvement.¹⁶⁵⁸

**Collateral Maintenance and Perfection Obligations**

The credit agreement requires United Environmental to (1) execute and deliver **UCC-1 financing statements** in all jurisdictions where UESC maintains tangible personal property, inventory, equipment, or accounts receivable, perfecting Administrative Agent's first-priority security interest under Article 9 of Uniform Commercial Code, with continuation statements filed before expiration of initial 5-year effectiveness period, (2) deliver **control agreements** for all deposit accounts, securities accounts, and commodity accounts under UCC § 9-104, providing Administrative Agent with ability to assume dominion over cash and investment accounts upon Event of Default without further action by UESC, (3) execute **mortgages and deeds of trust** on all real property with fair market value exceeding $10 million (54 facilities meeting threshold), recorded in appropriate county land records and accompanied by ALTA lender's title insurance policies with endorsements for comprehensive coverage, survey, access, zoning, and environmental lien protection, (4) provide **landlord waivers and access agreements** for all leased facilities, granting lenders right to access leased premises and continue operations following UESC bankruptcy or lease default, and (5) deliver **intellectual property security agreements** granting security interest in all patents, trademarks, trade names, and copyrights, recorded with United States Patent and Trademark Office to perfect lender interest against bona fide purchasers.¹⁶⁵⁹

United Environmental's collateral perfection demonstrates **material gaps** requiring immediate post-closing remediation: (1) UCC-1 continuation statements for 14 states lapsed in Q3 2024 (Arizona, Colorado, Connecticut, Kansas, Kentucky, Louisiana, Maryland, Minnesota, New Hampshire, Oklahoma, Oregon, South Carolina, Vermont, Wisconsin), creating **unperfected security interest exposure** for equipment and inventory valued at $342 million located in those jurisdictions and enabling competing secured creditors or bankruptcy trustee to obtain senior priority through subsequent perfection, (2) **12 controlled accounts** lack proper control agreements giving lenders immediate access rights (combined account balances $67 million as of September 30, 2024), constituting breach of credit agreement collateral requirements and enabling UESC to withdraw funds and transfer to unrestricted accounts outside lender control, (3) **mortgages not recorded** for 8 facilities acquired in last 18 months (Buffalo processing center, Denver transfer station, Miami sorting facility, Minneapolis MRF, Nashville truck maintenance facility, Philadelphia recycling center, San Jose transfer station, St. Louis processing center) with aggregate $218 million book value, leaving lenders as unsecured creditors for those properties and permitting UESC to grant senior mortgages to equipment lenders or sale-leaseback counterparties without lender consent, and (4) **landlord waivers outstanding** for 37 leased facilities representing 29% of United Environmental's operating footprint (47 of 127 total facilities are leased rather than owned), preventing lenders from accessing facilities or assuming leases in bankruptcy scenario, materially impairing going-concern liquidation value by eliminating operational continuity option.¹⁶⁶⁰

**Regulatory Compliance and Permit Maintenance Covenants**

The credit agreement requires United Environmental to (1) maintain **all material licenses and permits** necessary for waste collection, transportation, processing, and disposal operations in compliance with applicable federal, state, and local law, including (a) EPA Part B hazardous waste facility permits under 42 U.S.C. § 6925 for 23 TSDF facilities, (b) state solid waste facility permits for 89 collection and processing centers under respective state environmental codes, (c) Clean Air Act Title V operating permits for 12 facilities with major source emissions under 42 U.S.C. § 7661a, (d) NPDES stormwater discharge permits for 67 facilities under Clean Water Act Section 402, (e) DOT motor carrier operating authority for interstate waste transportation under 49 U.S.C. § 13902, and (f) local zoning and conditional use permits for all operating facilities, (2) maintain compliance with **environmental laws and regulations** and promptly notify Administrative Agent of any Environmental Claim (defined as written notice of potential liability exceeding $1 million) within 5 business days of receipt, (3) maintain compliance with **OSHA workplace safety regulations** under 29 U.S.C. § 651 et seq., including process safety management requirements under 29 C.F.R. § 1910.119 for facilities handling hazardous materials, (4) maintain compliance with **DOT vehicle safety regulations** under 49 C.F.R. Parts 350-399 including driver qualification, hours of service, vehicle maintenance, and hazardous materials transportation, and (5) provide lenders with copies of all **material correspondence** with federal, state, or local regulatory agencies within 10 business days of receipt, including EPA inspection reports, state enforcement notices, OSHA citations, DOT safety audit results, and zoning violation notices.¹⁶⁶¹

United Environmental's regulatory compliance status reveals **systematic violations** creating Event of Default exposure under credit agreement: (1) **Part B permit modifications pending** for 7 facilities (Chicago North TSDF, Detroit processing center, Houston Ship Channel facility, Los Angeles hazardous waste unit, Phoenix TSDF, Portland facility, Seattle processing center) where UESC initiated capacity expansions and process changes exceeding permitted parameters without obtaining EPA approval through Class 2 or Class 3 modification procedures under 40 C.F.R. § 270.42, creating unauthorized operation risk and potential $37,500 per day penalties under 42 U.S.C. § 6928(a), (2) **Title V permit deviations** for 4 facilities (Baltimore combustion unit, Birmingham processing center, Louisville recycling facility, San Antonio transfer station) where actual emissions exceeded permitted levels in 11 of last 12 months, requiring deviation reports under 40 C.F.R. § 70.6(a)(3)(iii) but not timely submitted to state air quality agencies (ranging from 23 to 67 days late), exposing UESC to permit revocation proceedings and $25,000-50,000 per day civil penalties under state clean air acts, (3) **NPDES permit exceedances** documented in 127 discharge monitoring reports filed Q1-Q3 2024, showing stormwater discharge violations at 34 facilities for parameters including total suspended solids, oil and grease, pH, and priority pollutants (metals, PAHs, volatile organics), with no timely corrective action plans submitted to state water quality agencies as required by general permits, creating potential $37,500 per day penalties under Clean Water Act Section 309(d) and third-party citizen suit exposure under Section 505, and (4) **DOT safety rating downgrade** from Satisfactory to Conditional (announced October 2024) based on compliance review identifying driver qualification violations (12% of 547 drivers lacking valid CDL or medical certificates), hours of service violations (347 logbook falsifications in 6-month sample), vehicle maintenance deficiencies (23% of inspected vehicles with out-of-service defects), and hazardous materials violations (improper shipping paper documentation for 67 shipments), subjecting UESC to operating authority suspension under 49 U.S.C. § 13905 if not upgraded within 12 months through safety improvement plan.¹⁶⁶²

**SECTION III.G.3 STATUS:** Subsection complete. Word count: ~2,400 words. Footnotes: 1652-1662 (11 footnotes). Next subsection: III.G.4 (Default Events and Cure Mechanisms).


#### III.G.4. Default Events and Cure Mechanisms: Acceleration Triggers and Lender Remedies

The credit agreement defines **eight categories of Events of Default** permitting lenders to (1) accelerate all outstanding obligations, (2) terminate lending commitments, and (3) exercise remedies under security agreements, potentially forcing United Environmental Services Corporation into bankruptcy reorganization or liquidation. These default provisions create **material acceleration risk** during the 36-month post-acquisition period when American Sustainability Partners' operational improvement initiatives remain incomplete and financial performance exhibits significant volatility.¹⁶⁶³

##### Payment Default

The credit agreement defines **payment default** as failure to pay (1) principal when due, whether at scheduled maturity, upon acceleration, or by mandatory prepayment, (2) interest within **three business days** of the scheduled payment date, or (3) any other amounts (fees, expenses, indemnification obligations) within **five business days** of written demand from Administrative Agent.¹⁶⁶⁴ Unlike typical commercial credit agreements permitting 30-day cure periods for non-principal payments, the **abbreviated grace periods** (3 days for interest, 5 days for other amounts) create heightened default risk when United Environmental Services Corporation experiences temporary liquidity constraints.¹⁶⁶⁵

**Payment Default Risk Analysis.** United Environmental Services Corporation's **0.88× initial Debt Service Coverage Ratio** (Section III.F.3 *supra*) and **$53 million revolving credit availability** (73% drawn) create material risk of payment default during the first 24 months post-acquisition if operational improvement initiatives fail to generate projected $154 million EBITDA enhancement.¹⁶⁶⁶ Specifically:

**Interest Payment Exposure.** Quarterly interest obligations total **$73.1 million** (Term Loan B: $58.5 million at SOFR+425 bps on $3.0 billion; Revolver: $14.6 million at SOFR+375 bps on $400 million average utilization), requiring **$292.4 million annual cash interest** on $315 million baseline EBITDA (92.7% cash flow absorption before capital expenditures, working capital, and taxes).¹⁶⁶⁷ The three-business-day cure period means United Environmental Services Corporation must maintain **minimum $75 million cash reserves** to avoid technical default if quarterly operating cash flow falls below interest obligations.¹⁶⁶⁸

**Mandatory Prepayment Default Risk.** Asset sale mandatory prepayment provisions (Section III.G.2 *supra*) requiring **100% of net proceeds** applied to Term Loan B within 10 business days create payment default exposure if American Sustainability Partners consummates the projected **$450 million transfer station portfolio divestiture** but temporarily deploys proceeds for working capital or other strategic purposes before remitting to lenders.¹⁶⁶⁹ The credit agreement contains **no discretionary prepayment basket** permitting temporary retention of asset sale proceeds, meaning any delay beyond the 10-business-day deadline constitutes immediate payment default with zero cure period.¹⁶⁷⁰

##### Financial Covenant Default

The credit agreement defines **financial covenant default** as failure to comply with the Maximum Total Net Leverage Ratio covenant or Senior Secured Leverage Ratio covenant as of the last day of any fiscal quarter, tested within **45 days** after quarter-end upon delivery of quarterly financial statements and compliance certificate.¹⁶⁷¹ Unlike payment defaults permitting brief cure periods, **financial covenant breaches trigger immediate Event of Default** upon Administrative Agent's determination that the compliance certificate demonstrates non-compliance, with **no grace period** for remediation.¹⁶⁷²

**Covenant Default Probability Assessment.** Section III.G.1 analysis demonstrates United Environmental Services Corporation's **pro forma Total Net Leverage Ratio** of **5.2×** (calculated using maximum permitted Adjusted EBITDA addbacks totaling $254 million) provides only **4.8-turn cushion** against the Year 1 covenant level of 10.0×.¹⁶⁷³ However, this cushion deteriorates rapidly under downside scenarios:

| Scenario | Pro Forma Leverage | Covenant Level | Cushion | Default Risk |
|----------|-------------------|----------------|---------|--------------|
| **Base Case** (100% operational improvements) | 5.2× | 10.0× | 4.8× | **Low** |
| **Downside Case** (60% operational improvements) | 7.8× | 10.0× | 2.2× | **Medium** |
| **Severe Downside** (25% operational improvements) | 11.4× | 10.0× | **(1.4×)** | **High (95% probability of Q3 2025 breach)** |

Under the Severe Downside scenario (Section III.F.6 *supra*), United Environmental Services Corporation would breach the Maximum Total Net Leverage Ratio covenant in **Q3 2025** (six months post-closing), triggering immediate Event of Default and potential acceleration of $3.0 billion debt obligations.¹⁶⁷⁴

**Equity Cure Right Limitations.** The credit agreement permits United Environmental Services Corporation to cure leverage covenant breaches through **equity cure contributions** (subordinated equity injections from American Sustainability Partners treated as Adjusted EBITDA for covenant calculation purposes), subject to stringent limitations: (1) **maximum two cures** during any four consecutive fiscal quarters, (2) **maximum five cures** during the term of the facility, (3) **minimum $50 million per cure** (representing 3.3% of ASP's $1.5 billion equity investment), and (4) cure contributions must be received within **15 business days** after delivery of non-compliant compliance certificate.¹⁶⁷⁵ These restrictions mean American Sustainability Partners can cure a maximum of **two consecutive quarterly breaches** before exhausting the four-quarter basket, creating **permanent covenant default** if operational improvements fail to materialize by the third consecutive quarter.¹⁶⁷⁶

##### Cross-Default Provisions

The credit agreement contains **comprehensive cross-default provisions** triggering Event of Default upon: (1) failure to pay principal or interest on **any other indebtedness** exceeding $25 million when due (after applicable grace periods), or (2) occurrence of any event permitting acceleration of **any other indebtedness** exceeding $25 million, whether or not such acceleration is actually declared.¹⁶⁷⁷ These provisions create **cascading default risk** where breach of covenants in equipment financing agreements, real estate mortgages, or other debt instruments automatically triggers default under the primary credit agreement even if Term Loan B payments remain current.¹⁶⁷⁸

**Cross-Default Exposure Analysis.** United Environmental Services Corporation's $42 million equipment financing (Section III.F.1 *supra*), secured by specific collection vehicles and processing equipment with **separate financial covenants** and **collateral maintenance requirements**, exceeds the $25 million cross-default threshold, meaning any payment default or covenant breach under equipment financing automatically triggers Event of Default under the $3.0 billion credit agreement.¹⁶⁷⁹ Additionally, **real property mortgages** at 54 facilities valued at $1.2 billion containing independent debt service coverage requirements and property maintenance covenants create multiple cross-default triggers.¹⁶⁸⁰

**Material Risk: Equipment Financing Cross-Default.** Equipment financing agreements typically contain **more stringent covenants** than corporate credit facilities, including (1) **collateral value maintenance** requiring equipment appraised value to exceed 115% of outstanding loan balance, tested semi-annually, (2) **individual asset DSCR requirements** mandating minimum 1.25× coverage calculated on revenue attributable to financed vehicles, and (3) **utilization covenants** requiring minimum 75% monthly route utilization.¹⁶⁸¹ United Environmental Services Corporation's aging fleet (average vehicle age: 9.2 years per Section III.E.5 *supra*) creates material risk that semi-annual appraisals could demonstrate collateral value below 115% threshold, triggering equipment financing default that cross-defaults into the primary credit agreement despite continued payment performance on the Term Loan B.¹⁶⁸²

##### Bankruptcy and Insolvency Defaults

The credit agreement defines **bankruptcy-related Events of Default** encompassing: (1) voluntary bankruptcy petition filing under Chapter 7 or Chapter 11 by United Environmental Services Corporation or any material subsidiary, (2) involuntary bankruptcy petition filing that remains undismissed for **60 days**, (3) appointment of receiver, trustee, or custodian for substantially all assets that remains undischarged for **60 days**, (4) general assignment for benefit of creditors, (5) admission in writing of inability to pay debts as they mature, or (6) board of directors adoption of resolution authorizing any of the foregoing actions.¹⁶⁸³ Notably, bankruptcy Events of Default create **automatic acceleration** with zero notice requirement, meaning lenders need not declare default or accelerate—the filing itself immediately accelerates all obligations.¹⁶⁸⁴

**Involuntary Bankruptcy Risk.** United Environmental Services Corporation's **extensive environmental liabilities** (Section III.E *supra*) totaling $89-267 million at Legacy Sites plus **contingent CERCLA exposure** at 34 additional potentially responsible party sites create material risk of **involuntary bankruptcy petition** by environmental creditors seeking priority treatment of cleanup obligations.¹⁶⁸⁵ Under 11 U.S.C. § 303(b), three creditors holding aggregate undisputed claims exceeding $18,600 may file involuntary Chapter 11 petition if debtor generally not paying debts as they become due.¹⁶⁸⁶ Environmental plaintiffs in the Riverside litigation ($89M settlement), Central Valley litigation ($47M exposure), and Puget Sound contribution action ($67M exposure) collectively hold $203 million claims exceeding the statutory threshold by 1,091%, creating realistic involuntary petition risk if United Environmental Services Corporation contests liability or delays settlement negotiations.¹⁶⁸⁷

The **60-day dismissal period** for involuntary petitions provides limited protection: even if United Environmental Services Corporation successfully moves to dismiss a meritless petition within 60 days, the **interim period** permits bankruptcy automatic stay to halt lender collection efforts, interfere with cash management arrangements, and disrupt business operations.¹⁶⁸⁸ More significantly, lender acceleration rights **vest immediately upon filing**, meaning even if the petition is later dismissed, lenders have already obtained the right to accelerate and may elect to maintain acceleration rather than waive the default.¹⁶⁸⁹

##### Material Adverse Change Default

The credit agreement defines **Material Adverse Effect** (MAE) Event of Default as occurrence of any event, change, or circumstance that has had or would reasonably be expected to have a **material adverse effect** on (1) the business, assets, operations, or financial condition of United Environmental Services Corporation and its subsidiaries taken as a whole, (2) the ability of borrower to perform payment obligations under loan documents, or (3) the rights and remedies of lenders under loan documents or the validity or enforceability of loan documents.¹⁶⁹⁰ Unlike acquisition agreements where MAE provisions typically contain extensive carve-outs for general economic conditions, industry-wide effects, and known matters,¹⁶⁹¹ credit agreement MAE Events of Default contain **no such qualifiers**, permitting lenders to declare default based on subjective determination that material adverse effect has occurred.¹⁶⁹²

**MAE Default Risk Scenarios.** Several developments during the 36-month post-acquisition period could constitute Material Adverse Effect Events of Default:

**Environmental Liability Escalation.** Discovery of **additional contamination** at Legacy Sites requiring remediation costs exceeding the $89-267 million reserve range by more than 50% (i.e., exceeding $400 million total) would likely constitute MAE affecting financial condition, particularly if such liability threatens covenant compliance or requires equity contributions exceeding American Sustainability Partners' $1.5 billion committed investment.¹⁶⁹³ The subjective MAE standard means lenders need not prove United Environmental Services Corporation is actually unable to pay—reasonable expectation of future payment inability suffices.¹⁶⁹⁴

**Regulatory License Suspension.** Suspension of **RCRA Part B permits** at the 23 TSDF facilities (representing 67% of treatment & disposal revenue per Section III.E.1 *supra*) due to unresolved permit modification applications (Section III.G.3 *supra*) would constitute MAE affecting business operations, as United Environmental Services Corporation would be legally prohibited from accepting hazardous waste shipments during suspension period.¹⁶⁹⁵ Even temporary 90-180 day suspensions could justify MAE declaration, as customer relationships would be permanently damaged by service interruptions.¹⁶⁹⁶

**DOT Operating Authority Revocation.** The Department of Transportation's October 2024 downgrade of UESC's safety rating from Satisfactory to Conditional (Section III.G.3 *supra*), combined with **operating authority suspension risk** if corrective actions prove insufficient, would constitute MAE affecting ability to perform operations.¹⁶⁹⁷ Without DOT motor carrier authority, United Environmental Services Corporation's 847-vehicle fleet could not legally transport waste in interstate commerce, eliminating **$2.1 billion collection revenue** (56% of total revenue per Section III.D.1 *supra*).¹⁶⁹⁸

##### Representation and Warranty Default

The credit agreement treats **material misrepresentations** in loan documents or compliance certificates as immediate Event of Default, specifically providing that if any representation, warranty, or certification made in loan documents or delivered pursuant to loan documents **proves to have been materially incorrect** when made or deemed made, such occurrence constitutes Event of Default.¹⁶⁹⁹ This provision creates **retrospective default risk** where initially accurate representations become false due to subsequent events, coupled with **certification risk** for CFO compliance certificates (Section III.G.3 *supra*) containing Adjusted EBITDA calculations.¹⁷⁰⁰

**Material Risk: Environmental Representation Breach.** The credit agreement requires United Environmental Services Corporation to represent that (1) all environmental liabilities have been disclosed, (2) borrower is in compliance with all environmental laws and permits, and (3) no environmental conditions exist that would reasonably be expected to result in material liability.¹⁷⁰¹ Discovery of **previously undisclosed contamination** at the 12 facilities with incomplete Phase II ESAs (Section III.E.2 *supra*) requiring remediation exceeding $25 million would render the environmental compliance representation materially false as of closing, triggering immediate Event of Default even if United Environmental Services Corporation promptly undertakes remediation.¹⁷⁰² The representation contains **no knowledge qualifier** (i.e., does not state "to borrower's knowledge"), meaning borrower warrants absolute compliance regardless of actual awareness.¹⁷⁰³

**Compliance Certificate Misstatement Risk.** CFO quarterly compliance certificates (Section III.G.3 *supra*) certifying compliance with financial covenants contain detailed **Adjusted EBITDA calculation schedules** showing all permitted addbacks under five categories totaling up to $254 million (Section III.G.1 *supra*).¹⁷⁰⁴ If lenders subsequently determine that specific addbacks were **improperly calculated** or did **not meet definitional requirements**, the compliance certificate would be deemed materially incorrect, constituting Event of Default.¹⁷⁰⁵ For example:

- **Pro Forma Adjustment Overstatement.** If UESC claims $67M pro forma cost savings from facility consolidation (Section III.G.1 *supra*), but lenders later determine that only $42M of such savings were actually "reasonably identifiable and factually supportable" per the addback definition, the $25M overstatement would render the compliance certificate materially false.¹⁷⁰⁶

- **Restructuring Charge Misclassification.** If UESC classifies $89M of operational expenditures as "restructuring charges" eligible for addback, but lenders determine such costs were routine operating expenses rather than one-time charges, the misclassification renders the certificate false and triggers default.¹⁷⁰⁷

The representation warranty default provision contains **zero cure period**—the default arises immediately upon discovery of the misrepresentation, with lender acceleration rights vesting automatically.¹⁷⁰⁸

##### Acceleration Mechanics and Lender Remedies

Upon occurrence and continuation of any Event of Default, **Required Lenders** (lenders holding majority of outstanding commitments and loans, calculated separately for Term Loan B and revolving credit facility) may (1) declare all outstanding obligations **immediately due and payable**, (2) terminate all lending commitments, and (3) exercise all rights and remedies under security agreements and guarantees.¹⁷⁰⁹ The credit agreement grants lenders **broad discretion** to accelerate, with no requirement to provide notice and opportunity to cure except for the specific grace periods described above for payment defaults.¹⁷¹⁰

**Payment Acceleration Impact.** Immediate acceleration of **$3.0 billion Term Loan B** plus **$400 million revolving credit borrowings** plus accrued interest, fees, and expenses totaling approximately **$3.45 billion** would create immediate liquidity crisis requiring United Environmental Services Corporation to (1) seek alternative refinancing (highly unlikely given covenant default triggering acceleration), (2) sell substantially all assets in distressed sale process (realizing significant discount to book value), or (3) file voluntary Chapter 11 bankruptcy petition to prevent liquidation.¹⁷¹¹ United Environmental Services Corporation's **$53 million revolving credit availability** and **$23 million cash balance** (Section III.F.4 *supra*) provide zero capacity to satisfy accelerated obligations.¹⁷¹²

**Collateral Foreclosure Remedies.** The credit agreement security agreement grants Administrative Agent (acting on behalf of lenders) **first-priority perfected security interests** in substantially all assets of United Environmental Services Corporation and subsidiaries, including accounts receivable, inventory, equipment, real property, intellectual property, and equity interests in subsidiaries (Section III.G.2 *supra*).¹⁷¹³ Upon acceleration, Administrative Agent may exercise all remedies under Article 9 of the Uniform Commercial Code and applicable real property foreclosure laws, including:

**Article 9 Public Sale.** Under UCC § 9-610, Administrative Agent may sell collateral at **public auction** after providing 10 days' notice to borrower, with sale proceeds applied to outstanding obligations in order of priority.¹⁷¹⁴ Collection accounts receivable ($267 million), equipment ($892 million), and inventory ($45 million) totaling **$1.2 billion book value** would likely realize only **40-60% of book value** in distressed liquidation sale (**$480-720 million recovery**), creating **$2.28-2.52 billion deficiency** for which American Sustainability Partners would be liable under equity pledge.¹⁷¹⁵

**Real Property Foreclosure.** The 54 mortgaged facilities valued at $1.2 billion book value (Section III.G.3 *supra*) would be sold through **judicial foreclosure** or **power-of-sale foreclosure** depending on state law, requiring 60-180 days notice and redemption periods.¹⁷¹⁶ Environmental contamination at foreclosed properties creates **lender successor liability risk** under CERCLA § 107(a), potentially causing lenders to **abandon contaminated collateral** rather than take title, reducing recoveries.¹⁷¹⁷

**Equity Pledge Foreclosure.** Administrative Agent holds **pledge of 100% of equity interests** in United Environmental Services Corporation owned by American Sustainability Partners, permitting Agent to conduct **UCC Article 9 sale** of pledged equity interests to third-party buyers.¹⁷¹⁸ However, given United Environmental Services Corporation's negative enterprise value post-default (liabilities exceeding assets), equity pledge would likely realize **zero recovery**, with all value captured through asset-level collateral foreclosure.¹⁷¹⁹

**Setoff Rights.** The credit agreement grants lenders **contractual setoff rights** permitting appropriation of any deposits, credits, or other property of United Environmental Services Corporation held by lender in any capacity to satisfy outstanding obligations.¹⁷²⁰ This means lenders may freeze and seize all **cash accounts maintained at lender institutions** (estimated $23 million per Section III.F.4), blocking United Environmental Services Corporation's access to operating liquidity and forcing immediate bankruptcy filing.¹⁷²¹

##### Forbearance Considerations and Workout Dynamics

Commercial lending practice demonstrates that lenders rarely exercise immediate acceleration upon first Event of Default, instead entering **forbearance negotiations** where borrower pays increased **default interest** (typically 200 basis points above standard pricing, meaning **11.75% for Term Loan B** versus 9.75% standard rate) in exchange for temporary waiver of default and opportunity to cure underlying issues.¹⁷²² However, forbearance agreements typically require borrower to: (1) acknowledge default, (2) provide enhanced financial reporting (monthly versus quarterly), (3) grant additional collateral or guarantees, (4) pay forbearance fees (**50-100 basis points** of outstanding principal, or **$15-30 million** on $3.0 billion debt), and (5) consent to **amendment fees** upon permanent waiver (**25-50 basis points**, or **$7.5-15 million**).¹⁷²³

**Forbearance Limitations.** Forbearance negotiations face significant constraints when Events of Default stem from **fundamental business deterioration** (as opposed to technical covenant breaches). Specifically, if United Environmental Services Corporation experiences actual **negative cash flow** requiring drawdown of remaining $53 million revolving credit availability, lenders have limited incentive to forbear because additional borrowings increase lender exposure without improving borrower creditworthiness.¹⁷²⁴ At the point where **operational cash flow falls below interest obligations** ($292.4 million annual interest per calculation above), United Environmental Services Corporation enters "death spiral" where continued operations consume remaining liquidity without generating sufficient cash to service debt, making **preemptive bankruptcy filing** the optimal strategy to preserve asset value through debtor-in-possession financing and Chapter 11 plan process.¹⁷²⁵

**Required Lender Consent Threshold.** The credit agreement defines "Required Lenders" as lenders holding **majority** of aggregate commitments and loans, meaning forbearance requires consent of lenders representing **$1.5 billion** of the $3.0 billion Term Loan B facility.¹⁷²⁶ If debt trades at distressed levels (e.g., 50-70 cents on dollar reflecting default risk), **distressed debt investors** may acquire positions specifically to block forbearance and force either (1) borrower bankruptcy filing enabling investors to credit-bid for assets, or (2) borrower equity contribution at enterprise value significantly below American Sustainability Partners' $1.5 billion initial investment.¹⁷²⁷ The lack of **sacred rights provisions** (requiring unanimous lender consent for material modifications) means Required Lenders can approve amendments over objections of minority lenders, but conversely means minority lenders cannot block forbearance approved by Required Lenders.¹⁷²⁸

**FINDING:** **HIGH PRIORITY.** The comprehensive Event of Default framework, combined with abbreviated cure periods, cross-default provisions, and subjective Material Adverse Effect standards, creates **material acceleration risk** during the 36-month post-acquisition period. Specifically: (1) **0.88× initial DSCR** and **three-business-day interest cure period** create payment default exposure if operational improvements fail to generate projected cash flow, (2) **leverage covenant cushion of 4.8 turns** deteriorates to **(1.4×) breach** under Severe Downside scenario by Q3 2025, triggering potential acceleration of $3.0 billion debt, (3) **cross-default** to $42 million equipment financing and $1.2 billion mortgages creates cascading default risk from subsidiary-level covenant breaches, (4) **involuntary bankruptcy** risk from $203 million environmental creditor claims exceeding 11 U.S.C. § 303 threshold, (5) **MAE default discretion** permitting lender acceleration based on subjective assessment of regulatory license suspensions or contamination discoveries, (6) **representation warranty default** from retrospective falsity of environmental compliance representations upon discovery of undisclosed contamination at 12 facilities with incomplete Phase II ESAs, and (7) **forbearance limitations** reducing lender incentive to waive defaults once operational cash flow turns negative. American Sustainability Partners should negotiate (i) **extended cure periods** (30 days for interest payments versus 3 days standard), (ii) **equity cure baskets** permitting unlimited cures in first 12 months, (iii) **MAE definition carve-outs** for disclosed environmental matters and regulatory proceedings, and (iv) **cross-default thresholds** increased from $25 million to $100 million to exclude equipment financing and most mortgages.¹⁷²⁹


#### III.G.5. Priority Finding Summary: Aggregate Covenant Compliance Risk and Negotiation Strategy

The comprehensive analysis of the credit agreement covenant framework across financial maintenance requirements (III.G.1), incurrence-based restrictions (III.G.2), affirmative obligations (III.G.3), and default events (III.G.4) reveals **material covenant compliance risk** during the 36-month post-acquisition period when American Sustainability Partners' operational improvement initiatives remain partially implemented and financial performance exhibits significant volatility.
